Dear All,

This post is just an early message to those of you who, like me, still have a hankering for a BIG Rebel Snowspeeder to add to their collection.

Whilst I don't want to be offering an " all blow and no show" post I thought with all the current activity on the SW studioscale front it was worth staking a claim to this one early on. However if this note prompts someone to say they have already got a snowspeeder ready to roll, then I'd rather find that out now.

Currently kitpart ID'ing is the order of the day, but I'm pleased to say that ALOT of the key stuff has been nailed already. Only a couple of more prominent parts remain and then I can start drawing up plans. However, I have the great talent of Dan (1138) Satterthwaite working with me on this and he is of course an expert in such things. Its great to have his support again. Alongside Dan I also have another 'consultant' who is offering some great insights into this particular model. 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

What I hope to produce is a model that matches the common 21" speeder used in the film. Features I'm intending to include will be moveable airbrakes, both pilot figures and a stand. Currently my plan is to replicate the actual ILM model cockpit rather than do a synthesis of model and live action set. If all goes well and I get the speeder sorted I'd also like to include a scale version of the rebel anti-personnel turret....but I'm not making any promises on that yet.

So there you have it. That's the "Blow" out the way. Next time I hope to have something to "Show". I'm a ways off yet, but getting there as long as life permits me. -  If anyone would like to use this thread to express an interest in such a model, that would be a useful guide for me later on.

Happy building out there.

N

Hi Guys,

We are up to 10+ kits so far, but fortunately a few of those kits are offering alot of parts. The areas we need to tackle next are the forward gun bulkheads. I will confer with Dan over these areas to see if he thinks he has any leads. Dan's kit archive is waaay bigger than mine and he's got a great eye. If we do come up empty I'm happy to throw it open to anyone who can offer a match. Basically the quicker I can finish the ID stage the quicker I can get stuck into the patterns. What I want to avoid is the process I ended up going through on the Y-wing where I was building, then we found new parts that then showed up slight inaccuracies...so I had to re-build etc etc. 

With the T-47 I want to nail all the key details, and especially ones that give key dimensional references, up front so that when I draw the plans I know its dead on, end of story. Goodnight

I'm glad this project has piqued folks interest. So far no one has popped up saying they have beaten us to it so that's good. I've always loved the Snowspeeder and I'm going to do my best to get as close to an ILM stage model as I can. I've got some great support on this one so I'm confident we will produce something worthy and very accurate.  - Mind you I'm already having bad dreams about the underside. :cry

Things will probably go a bit quiet now as Dan and I plod on. Will post up progress/ answer questions when I can.

All the best

Nick

Hi Guys,

Calling all kitbash experts..

I've been trying to keep this project nudging along in between some other 'official' pattern work I'm doing. Got one more job to get shot of and then its big Snowspeeder time. - however in order to get it all sorted I could do with a little bit of help.

While I'm finishing this other job I wanted to ask if any of you kitbashing experts out there can help Dan and I with one niggly area that remains unidentified. I've attached a pic which shows areas in red and yellow that need a positive ID. I've got pretty much everything else important already nailed, and thus am ready to draw up plans etc. If anyone can help with these stragglers that would help move it all along nicely.

Needless to say the way I've highlighted the parts may not reflect their actual shape, layout etc. Yellow parts look to be from a ship maybe?

[attachmentid=10766]

Any help much appreciated  
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

Hi Michael,

I've sent you a PM. Thanks for your support and I'll say again in the open what a great job you've done with your T47. Like I said before you have put more greeblies on yours than ILM did.

I hope to make mine the definitive T47 in terms of accuracy to the ILM models. I'm also looking to incorporate working airbrakes and turning pilot head. I've designed mechanisms to accomplish this, but time will tell whether is feasible to include them in a kit without making it all too complicated to produce.

Still, aim high as I like to say :

Ya I think it would be mad expensive I wanted to run a couple servos with a control board in mine but I didn't start the project with this in mind.I was tempted but I know better, if it's not incorporated from the beginning you can run into trouble :angry You would need no less than at least one servo or two and a control board to operate them, also some kind of AC adapter.Considering MR's is $600.00 and yours going to be bigger and definitive it's going to be mad expensive as a kit alone with no electronics.Trust me though there will be a few people who will step up and want a non-static example of a 47. 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]
 I will make a better one with  all the works 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]
 Can't wait to see you get started on yours.....

Regards,

Michael

Re: Echo Station 57, we're on our way....slowly

I just wanted to put a post up to let anyone who's interested know that a full studio scale T-47 Snowspeeder is still in the works. I've not been able to touch it for months due to other things, but will aim to keep moving it forward, albeit slowly from now on.

My intentions are still to supply the model with adjustable airbrakes and two pilot figures. It will be 25% bigger than the MR Speeder so its going to be a fairly big model...

Small Pic here shows the Ertl kit for scale ref. Needless to say I'm not using it for build dimensions... I have much better reference than that 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]
 ( have not posted pics here for a while so I hope it works)

I'm going to fast prototype up some componants such as the guns which are all ready to be SLA'd up. More info as it happens, my next area to tackle is the cockpit tub.

N

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Echo Station 57, we're on our way....slowly

Just a quick update to show the hull is coming together. You can't see the panels and rivet marks very well here, but they are there...and very accurate.

My plan now is to have the top and bottom hull sections in Fibreglass probably with the airbrake boxes integral to the top section. (However I still hope to have the airflaps moveable) Other parts, including pilots will be in good old resin.

Next phase will be the cockpit interior which will be quite time consuming, but fun! - also when funds permit I will get the guns SLA'd up. 

Will update again as soon as I can.

N

http://i306.photobucket.com/albums/nn256/Gort_99/T-47 Studio Scale/Speeder_hull_2_s.jpg

http://i306.photobucket.com/albums/nn256/Gort_99/T-47 Studio Scale/Speeder_hull_s.jpg

Re: Echo Station 57, we're on our way....slowly

Hi Folks,

Another update on the T47. I did say I was doing the cockpit next, but I changed my mind. I've decided to do the underside instead as its a tricky part of the build that I wanted to know I had nailed. 

The small airflow fins that sit under the nose will be added later.

Hope you like it....

Post #37  (forum post #610041)
Author    : Gort
Date      : Jun 20, 2008 at 4:12 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Echo Station 57, we're on our way....slowly

Hi Guys,

Glad you like the story so far.

I'm with you there Lee, I've always loved the Speeder from the first moment they all whine and buzz into shot in Empire, then peel off across the mountains. Lovely stuff. - Think I will do the cockpit area next while I finalise any last kit finds.

As far as the moulding, casting and distribution goes I'm going to do the whole thing myself. As we have all seen, when you lose control of a project its very hard to get it back. I shall be the only one responsible for how this turns out, good, bad or indifferent!

I'm not sure how many of these I will shift, but I'll do a batch of 10 and see who comes along. I've noted the interest already shown here which I thank you for. I shall also offer build ups if there are any requests for such. And, needless to say in the current economic climate I will try and keep the unit cost down as much as possible. 

Anyway, must go and rummage in my kit box archive again!

Cheers

Nick

Post #60  (forum post #630390)
Author    : Gort
Date      : Jul 19, 2008 at 10:15 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Echo Station 57, we're on our way....slowly

Wow, I've just checked in to see if anyone liked the latest work...er, I take it that's a yes then! - many thanks for the kind words. Its all very encouraging.

I wanted to go for a mixture of the studio model cockpit tub, but jazzed up with aspects of the practical live action set. I think as the cockpit area is such a focal part of the Speeder, any display model would need it to be as detailed as possible to hold interest. So, it will build up nice out of the box..but if you are a demon superdetailer ( Jason?) there's plenty of scope to amp it up to the next level.

Kurt, re size. I'm not at home at the mo' to take exact measurements, but its about 55cm long and a bit less in width. So, basically it kind of fills a two foot square area.

Dan S: is that you? - long time no hear. Thanks for your assistance with the planning of this project...it took a while but I'm getting there 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

It still feels like there is a long road to go yet, I'll be happy once I get a good set of castings etc. I'm aiming for a decent pre-Xmas deadline.

I've been logging those interested in getting a Speeder in the order they have contacted/announced interest, so keep 'em coming!. - Nothing will happen till I have all the required kits boxed and ready to go though. No pre-payments etc. It gets too messy.

Cheers

Nick

Post #76  (forum post #631260)
Author    : Gort
Date      : Jul 21, 2008 at 1:06 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Nick... YOU ROCK!!!

Stormy320 said:

			That is very impressive. Do you have some insane reference pictures or are you taking some liberties? Either way it is awesome.
		

Click to expand...

 

I do have very good reference pics, but as I mentioned in a previous post the actual ILM filming models (at the size I'm making here) had a more basic interior than I felt a replica display version required. 

That said, I have included studio accurate kit parts in what I've made, but I've also taken some cues from the full size set and melded the two together. I am going to be supplying two pilot figures as well, but I'll do those after I've nailed the main ship patterns, as they are purely sculptural.

Nick
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
Post #77  (forum post #645764)
Author    : Gort
Date      : Aug 8, 2008 at 1:13 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Echo Station 57, we're on our way....slowly

Hi there Speeder fans,

Just a quick note to impart a good news, bad news message. Good news is I'm 99% done on the rear of the Snowspeeder. That covers 

The engine section details

The Engine cooling fins,, inc the harpoon cable fixing point

The areas around the rear airbrake control struts

The rear airbrakes assemblies themselves.

Bad news, is that I go away on holiday now and havn't got time to take and post the pics of all the new patterns. So, I guess I'm just letting you know that progress is good but the pics to prove it are about 2 weeks away.

NB: As promised the rear airbrakes are fully poseable by virtue of two simple rigs that use small but strong magnets. This way they can operate on a constant friction basis and can be set any way you like. Now I've proved it works on the lower airbrakes I hope to do something similar for the upper flaps. The lack of space will make this a bit tricky but I'm going to do my best :confused

Cheers

Nick

Re: Echo Station 57, we're on our way....slowly

The pricing will have to be finalised once I get to the end of the line but I am trying to bring it in around the $300 -$350 mark. As you say Kurt, its quite a big model and with moveable airflaps and two figures I think it will be a pretty good deal. 

To be honest I'm really surprised, and delighted, that so many people share my desire to own a big Speeder! - With all these expectant faces metaphorically pressed up against my window, I'm starting to feel the pressure! :lol 

I think for me once I know I have got a full set of good quality casts out and can deliver the kit I want to deliver I'll relax a bit! - 

Thanks for the continued support folks! 

Nick

Click to expand...

 

Hi, Glad you like the show so far 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

If you don't want figures I can supply without, but as has been pointed out its not really going to affect the bottom line cost. The major fly in your ointment though is that 1/6th figures will be too big. ILM did custom sculpts. I'm going to do the pilots myself and it will be a case of eyeballing the ILM ref to see what looks right rather than just making a figure of a particular scale. However they are looking to be around 1/7th - 1/8th, but until I get to that stage I'm not 100% decided.

I'm just now working out the rigs for the top airflaps...oooh my brain hurts :wacko

Re: Echo Station 57, we're on our way....slowly

Hi,

See below for the latest work in progress shots. All I have to make now are the face panels for the forward gun bulkheads, the harpoon gun and of course the pilots. Had wanted to get the gun panels finished for this update, but I've had too many other things crop up.

Needless to say the parts are just propped/taped in place and the top and bottom hulls are not mated up as they would be etc.

Anyway, hope you like 'em....

NB: The actual gun barrels will be pre-cut plastic tubing.

Re: Echo Station 57, we're on our way....slowly

Hi Kurt,

In all honesty, I don't know. I'm pushing as hard as I can to keep the project moving forward in between other 'proper' work, but its like having two jobs at the moment. I am behind where I wanted to be at this point. i.e I had hoped to be onto moulding and casting end of Sept, but I've a bit more to do now before that.

I'm keen to get some kits sold before Xmas as I need to start re-couping my investment, but equally I don't want to rush it now and screw up what seems to be working well thus far. Like I've said before I never anticipated such a big interest in the project and the expectations that go along with that, but its great to hear such a positive reaction from people and I want to make sure I deliver you all something special. - Lee I'm really glad I've helped you back into your childhood a bit. I feel the same when I'm building. Especially with the Empire soundtrack filling the workshop 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

I'll just keep forging ahead and see how far I can get. Thanks again for all the supportive comments!

Nick

Post #155  (forum post #687314)
Author    : JPolacchi
Date      : Oct 6, 2008 at 11:49 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Echo Station 57, we're on our way....slowly

In modern day film making,CGI has it uses.Most often,due to the complexity of the FX shot,it would be incredibly difficult(if not impossible) to achieve the desired look/finished shot.Plus,you have these huge FX films comming out every summer(or every other summer),each one trying to outdue the last film that was released.However,I agree...nothing compares to the depth that a finely constructed film miniature can achieve,and even with the biggest budget FX films and the best CGI tech geeks emoployed,I can still spot CGI effects and they don't come close to a model.I both despise and admire CGI work,but models offer so much more and I've yet to see a film made today that can achieve the same things that films of 20-30 years ago had achieved.Case in piont,the opening scene of Star Wars.I was forever mesmorized at 4 1/2 years old when I saw that and it is pernamentally engrained into my memory.Models rule!CGI is just a good stand in when the impossible is required.

Post #159  (forum post #696322)
Author    : Gort
Date      : Oct 20, 2008 at 12:41 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Echo Station 57, we're on our way....slowly

Heh, heh. Thanks Guys. Don't worry the Surrey Skunkworks are still working away. I got totally slammed at work last week, but managed to claw some time back over the weekend. Have got the detailing for the gun bulkheads done now and am moving onto the harpoon gun. After that the ships itself is done. Pics will follow on in a week or so for all of the above.

I want to do at least the Pilot heads & flight helmets in Zbrush. I've been wanting to use it to originate an STL file for a while now and this seems a nice simple one to kick off with. 

BTW ( blatant plug) check out this link to the EVE online game store. 

http://store.eve-online.com/

I created a range of collectible spacecraft based on their in-game designs ( which are quite cool actually). They are meant to be real world versions of the virtual ships that the players are zooming across the stars in. The patterns were a mixture of SLA prototyping and good old fashioned styrene bashing!
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

Nick

Post #160  (forum post #696353)
Author    : Eric Ladd
Date      : Oct 20, 2008 at 1:20 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Echo Station 57, we're on our way....slowly

I am so eagerly awaiting your kit I can't explain it. Back when I was MUCH younger, living in Georgia, I built an AMT Snowspeeder with a smoke bomb and a fire cracker in the back of the model. I ran two strands of fishing line about 60 feet off the top rail of my front porch all the way down to the edge of my front yard. I set the speeder on the lines, lit the fuse and let go of the model when smoke started pouring out of the back. Tilting the lines up and down the speeder waived its wing tips, smoke billowing out the back, it hit the grass and stakes at the bottom of the run, sat about 1 second then exploded into a million pieces all over my front yard. I was slack jawed, wide eyed and from that time on the snowspeeder was THE most beautiful ship in my heart from the Star Wars universe. My only regret is not having a camera to actually film my first special effect. I might be exagerating, but it was gorgeous.

I am really looking forward to your kit. And I will NOT be blowing it up! :lol
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Echo Station 57....Updated

Hi Speeder fans,

As promised, please see 9 pics that show the recently completed pilot, gunner, harpoon gun and main blaster front bulkheads, plus, the lower hull mould which has turned out quite well. 

There are still a few adjustments to make to various things but hopefully you can get the general idea. 

With the pilots finished that really is the last of the construction over. I intend to start the top hull mould next and carry on from there. I'll post updates of castings as and when I can, though I'm still trying to keep things moving along as fast as I can in between work and life committments!

Hope you like it....

N

Re: Echo Station 57, we're on our way....slowly

Thanks guys. Glad you approve. The pilots truncate at the waist in the same way the ILM figures do. Infact these pilots have slightly more body and detail than the ILM originals. The ILM figures didn't have the pilots chest boxes which I have included.

I can't give an exact timescale as to when I will actually be able to sell finished kits as there are too many demands on my time at the moment, but I will be making a big dent in the moulding work this side of Xmas. I'll just have to hope you guys save some pennies for the New Year!

Nick

Post #210  (forum post #796024)
Author    : Gort
Date      : Feb 14, 2009 at 3:53 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Echo Station 57, we're on our way....slowly

Hi guys,

Thanks for the continued interest...and patience!

Here are a couple of pics of some test castings and the moulds I've done so far, just to show that though it may be quiet on the thread I am still slogging away. I've kicked off with the one part moulds and after I finish this note I'm back down to start claying up the first of the 2 part moulds. 

I reckon the final part count will be around 75+, ( gulp!) which means I have another 17 moulds to make ( groan). The biggest pain is having to redo the main hull moulds. They turned out ok for a couple of quick and dirty casts but weren't quite up to mass production. So, I'll do those again as the last job before launching into casting properly.

Just so I know, if anyone who has contacted me for a kit has decided, or realised through circumstances that they really can't stick with it please drop me a pm so I can update my records and keep a realistic list of names etc. 

Hey Kurt, glad to hear from you again. Was getting worried you had got bored with me! 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

Cheers

Nick

Post #213  (forum post #796056)
Author    : Gort
Date      : Feb 14, 2009 at 5:42 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Echo Station 57, we're on our way....slowly

Thanks guys. I'm experimenting on some parts, especially the larger more detailed pieces, with a combination of slush cast PU resin, GRP gelcoats backed with PU resins, and slow cure PU that I can hand work the bubbles out of. 

Its funny, when you are doing stuff like this the threat of air bubbles becomes the all consuming bane of your existence! - ironic really as the original ILM speeder castings (of the size I'm making) have lots of blown out details and little bubbles holes. Which of course wasn't a problem as they never showed up etc.

Nick

Post #215  (forum post #796220)
Author    : JPolacchi
Date      : Feb 14, 2009 at 10:22 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Echo Station 57, we're on our way....slowly

I should think that a first pour and slush cast would allieviate a good 95%-99% of surface bubbles.From my standpoint,I'd steer away from gel coats or any pollyester resins just because they shrink so damm much (a minimum of 10%).You can/should be able to do consecutive pours with pollyurethane resins,a slush cast followed by a solid pour.Just be sure that when casting with a urethane that there is no residual moisture or humidity because then you with get lots of bubbles/frothing as urethans react violently with water.Another idea is if you just want to have a urethane shell or to keep a certain part relatively hollow,you can do the slush mold (get a good .020-.030 shell)then lay in fiberglass w/epoxy for rigitity and strength.Epoxy hardly shrinks at all as does urethan resins.I think they shrink around 1%-2% and not like pollyesters.
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Post #218  (forum post #796409)
Author    : Gort
Date      : Feb 14, 2009 at 2:36 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Echo Station 57, we're on our way....slowly

Hi,

Thanks for the advice, always welcome 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]
. I agree that the polyester resins are not the most user friendly. I have had some reasonable results from doing a gel coat backed with PU, but I wasn't planning on using it for the main kit runs. I'm trying to do it all now with three types of PU: a quick 5 min cure for shooting smaller 'fire and forget' moulds, then a slush cure and a slow (10min) cure for the larger more labour intensive parts. The main hull halves are the tricky ones as they are pretty big. 

Cheers

Nick

JPolacchi said:

			I should think that a first pour and slush cast would allieviate a good 95%-99% of surface bubbles.From my standpoint,I'd steer away from gel coats or any pollyester resins just because they shrink so damm much (a minimum of 10%).You can/should be able to do consecutive pours with pollyurethane resins,a slush cast followed by a solid pour.Just be sure that when casting with a urethane that there is no residual moisture or humidity because then you with get lots of bubbles/frothing as urethans react violently with water.Another idea is if you just want to have a urethane shell or to keep a certain part relatively hollow,you can do the slush mold (get a good .020-.030 shell)then lay in fiberglass w/epoxy for rigitity and strength.Epoxy hardly shrinks at all as does urethan resins.I think they shrink around 1%-2% and not like pollyesters.

Re: Echo Station 57, we're on our way....slowly

Hi,

Here a couple of pics showing some more castings. The engine cooling fins have turned out well, and I'm very pleased with the rather tricky lower airbrake supports. 

NB: The engine bulkhead is just an old GRP test cast and the fins have just been push fitted into place for the purposes of the pic.

Also got the main gun barrels sorted, and the canopy hinges, plus the seat and a couple of parts for the gunners station.

Next up and awaiting their second pour of RTV are the airbrake flaps top & bottom, the angled gun bulkead covers, two pipes for the engine area and a couple more cockpit sections including the dashboard.

Hope you approve

Post #271  (forum post #884744)
Author    : Gort
Date      : May 27, 2009 at 1:42 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Echo Station 57, we're on our way....slowly

Hi,

For those following this thread this is just a quick note to apologise for the quiet patch lately. I got messed about by my resin and RTV supplier which meant I missed out on a few days where I had planned to get on with the main hulls. Lately I've had hardly any chance to work on things.

I am on the case again now though, and have a top hull cast up. What I've decided to do is re work the mould that forms the top trailing edge of the top hull. Basically Luke's speeder has flat areas, whilst Wedge and the other 'Red' marked speeders have a set of ridges that extend out. I want to be able to swap these reverse moulds so that I can cast up whichever version folk want rather than have to have folks apply these ridges as part of the build up.

So....bear with me and I will get some pics up again soon. 

Cheers

Nick

Post #279  (forum post #895526)
Author    : Gort
Date      : Jun 7, 2009 at 5:21 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Echo Station 57, we're on our way....slowly

An update from Echo Base....

Here are some pics showing the development work I've been doing on the main hull sections. They are made from epoxy and reinforced with an epoxy paste impregnated with carbon fibres. The beauty of the paste is that you can apply it very easily and sculpt it to form support bulkheads. Though its very strong its also very easy to dremel away should anyone want to; eg lighting, or cutting away hull panels for superdetailing etc. I've still got a bit more tinkering before they all mate up properly but I'm getting there.

I did a test to see how I can create the ridges on the trailing edges of the top hull and one pics shows this. For some reason the epoxy on this cast was still soft so the part got deformed, but it served it purpose.

http://i306.photobucket.com/albums/nn256/Gort_99/T-47 Studio Scale/Lower_hull_kit.jpg

http://i306.photobucket.com/albums/nn256/Gort_99/T-47 Studio Scale/Mainhulls_epoxy_paste.jpg

http://i306.photobucket.com/albums/nn256/Gort_99/T-47 Studio Scale/Mainhulls_epoxy_paste_2.jpg

I've done some pilot castings which have turned out well. Also I've taped up an airbrake box to the top hull to show how that all looks. NB For the sharp eyed out there you'll notice the front grill on this particular hull cast has blow outs, however other casts have come out perfectly. I'd just skimmed the epoxy over it on this one, infact I need to squish the stuff into the surface with my finger and it comes out fine.

http://i306.photobucket.com/albums/nn256/Gort_99/T-47 Studio Scale/Pilots_1.jpg

http://i306.photobucket.com/albums/nn256/Gort_99/T-47 Studio Scale/Pilots_hand.jpg

http://i306.photobucket.com/albums/nn256/Gort_99/T-47 Studio Scale/Mainhull_rear.jpg

http://i306.photobucket.com/albums/nn256/Gort_99/T-47 Studio Scale/Tophull__airbrake_1.jpg

http://i306.photobucket.com/albums/nn256/Gort_99/T-47 Studio Scale/Tophull__airbrake_2.jpg

There is a pic showing the airflap rig that I intend to offer. It simply involves some magnets and magnetic strip which enables the airflap to be held in an open position for those who may want to alternate between a deployed/closed display stance. The plan is to have the same system for the lower brakes.

http://i306.photobucket.com/albums/nn256/Gort_99/T-47 Studio Scale/Airbrake_magnet_rig.jpg

I should just say that as of tomorrow, 8th June I'm starting a pretty heavyweight new job so my head is going to be groaning with all the new stuff I have to deal with. I'll keep plugging away at the Speeder but I'm not sure at the moment how much of an impact the new job will have on my evenings etc. 

Anyway, hope you like the pics, I'll hopefully get a proper set of castings done soon in order to do a full build up.

Cheers

Nick

Post #295  (forum post #912560)
Author    : Gort
Date      : Jun 25, 2009 at 1:25 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Echo Station 57, we're on our way....slowly

Hi folks,

Here is a quick pic to give you an idea of the number of parts involved in this thing. Final count is probably north of 97...which is waaay more than I had originally hoped for at the outset of the project. Gulp...

http://i306.photobucket.com/albums/nn256/Gort_99/T-47 Studio Scale/Full_set_casts_s.jpg

I just realised I forgot to include the canopy hinges, but I've shown you pics of those already.

I'm going to try and actually build one up next, not to any great display standard but just to check it works out ok and of course do an instruction sheet etc. Then I will start to contact my list in groups of 5 as I want to break it up into manageable chunks. 

I will also need to do a final tally on costs. I've said for a while that I want to keep around the $400 mark, and I still hope I do, but I've spent alot more on silicone and materials than I planned in order to make the hull moulds and develop kit, which has been part of my learning curve.

At the end of the day I would rather sell less and cover my costs than kill myself and take a big hit. 

Anyway, I don't plan to drop any massive bombshells costwise but just wanted to warn you guys in case my numbers don't look good. 

Updates will follow again soon.

Nick

Post #311  (forum post #935493)
Author    : Gort
Date      : Jul 19, 2009 at 4:59 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Echo Station 57, we're on our way....slowly

Hi Guys,

I've been getting really hammered with work pressures and family committments lately. Have not had as much time to work on the speeder as I would have liked. However I am making progress. The first build up has the engine,canopy, cockpit and pilots all done, plus the lower air brakes. I'm having to photo what I'm doing for the instructions which takes a bit of time too.

Next up is the upper airbrake boxes and the guns. I'll then give it a quick paintjob and post some pics. Its tempting to show you what I've done so far as I'm quite pleased with how the pilots and cockpit is looking...however, I'm going to hold fire so that the pictures I post are the completed speeder. No more progress, just a finished model. 

Watch this space....

Re: Echo Station 57, we're on our way....slowly

'ATTACK PATTERN DELTA, GO NOW!'

Here is first build up. Due to chronic lack of time I've had lately I kinda flung this together. Its certainly not built to display standards, but it proved that the kit works which is all I wanted to do, plus provide pics for the instructions. Don't be too harsh on my paint job, again done very fast!.

This is a basic straight out the box build. I hope and expect that you guys will go to town in the cockpit and add straps and details and even fibre optics! 
[IMAGE: yH5BAEAAAAALAAAAAABAAEAAAIBRAA7]

Anyway, hope you like it. I've got to dash out now to take my boys out for the day. Will check in later to read the verdicts...gulp! :confused

Post #355  (forum post #961434)
Author    : Gort
Date      : Aug 17, 2009 at 2:08 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Echo Station 57, we're on our way....slowly

Cheers Jamie. Really glad the final pictures have gone down well.

I'm making one kit up to be sent over to the States where a colleague has agreed to help me size up the decals. I've also got to make up the instructions sheet PDF, which I'll do once the kit is sent off.

After that I will contact the first 5 or so folks on my list and start the ball rolling. The main issue for me will be the pure time it takes to make up all the parts. Especially the hulls and airbrake boxes which require epoxy gel coating and reinforcement, which takes 24hrs to cure. 

I'm finalising the cost over the course of the above work.

Stay tuned....

Nick

Post #367  (forum post #980369)
Author    : Gort
Date      : Sep 10, 2009 at 3:29 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Echo Station 57, we're on our way....slowly

Thanks.

I've just been producing my second set of pulls and de-bugging the moulding process a bit more. I'm not set up like some of the others on the board like Steve N in terms of vacuum/pressure casting and its quite a challenge to produce parts up to the spec I want. A few parts are actually quite a pig to do.

I'm also 3/4 of the way through the instructions. I really want these done up front so I can email over the pdf's before the kit arrives so folks can start to peruse what they will be getting. I've also ordered the sets of magnets used in the airbrake rigs, and the boxes for shipping. Need to sort out the best way to package things etc

I will be contacting the first people on my list in the next couple of weeks - just hope folks still have some hard earned cash left to splash!

Nick

Post #389  (forum post #995237)
Author    : Gort

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Echo Station 57, we're on our way....slowly

I've just started to contact the first people on my list, and to make the first kits so the ball is rolling at last. Cost has ended up $430+ shipping. That will include decals.

NB: I'm going to organise things in the following way.

Contact people to confirm order & details

Wait 2 weeks for a response. If none received I will offer their kit to the next person in the queue and so on.

Once I reach the end of the main list I will contact people on the backup list.

If people do get in touch after the 2 week window I will still supply a kit but they will have lost their place in the queue.

This seems the fairest way to go and keeps my cashflow moving! - Hope everyone is ok with this.

As this thread has effectively come to an end in terms of building/updates I will not post any further messages here but possibly start something in the Junkyard or just communicate with individuals.

Cheers

Nick

Re: Echo Station 57, we're on our way....slowly

I got the test casting today, and will size the markings to the kit, so everyone can have awesome decals!

This kit BLOWS MY MIND. Seriously. I have no idea what was used to cast the upper and lower shells (and main engine bits) but it's like some sort of super-lightweight fiberglass. Strong, CRISPLY CAST, square and true. 

All of the resin parts are equally well cast. Plus, the pilot/gunner are awesome and look like they're doing the robot. Heh. The arrival/timing was perfect too - Wynnstudio, SDStudios, and JTGraphics were over today, and everyone agreed that it kicks ass. There are a few very minor areas that need a smidge of filler, but no one but the Japanese make perfect castings, hehe.  

Gort - you have NOTHING to fear if this is indicative of what everyone else is going to get.

Post #401  (forum post #1007319)
Author    : Gort
Date      : Oct 11, 2009 at 1:39 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Echo Station 57, we're on our way....slowly

Thanks Jason. As I mentioned the hulls you got were a bit of a Beta Test and I've optimised things a bit better for the ones I'm doing now. The hulls and airbrake boxes are an Epoxy gel coat backed up up with a carbon fibre reinforced epoxy paste. Strong but light.

The hulls actually have a bit of flex in them which helps in the build. Everyone should note that though strong the hulls are more brittle than say the same thing done in PU. Take care with the edges of the hulls till they are fixed together. As they are epoxy a bit of milliput will sort out any filing issues.

Hope it goes together ok.

Nick

Post #410  (forum post #1009457)
Author    : Gort
Date      : Oct 13, 2009 at 1:56 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Echo Station 57, we're on our way....slowly

Thanks guys. I'm refining the casting of the parts now so I'm getting quite quick at it. That said, with each kit having 100+parts its still quite a job. The top and lower hull alone take up a whole evening to lay up and then I have to leave them for about 36hrs. Shame my new job has coincided with all this as I'm totally knackered  :confused

I'm currently working on 4 kits which cover the first two people on my list, then I'm dropping back to doing just 2 kits at once ( Next 2 are for you Kurt). With four full sets of parts I simply don't have enough room to lay them out! These hulls are pretty large.

I can start to feel myself getting into a bit of a groove now, I think limiting myself to two at once will make things more manageable and actually speed up my turnaround.

PS: I'm gonna need a BIG rest after this before I think about an Awing!

Stay tuned

Nick

Post #430  (forum post #1121560)
Author    : Gort
Date      : Feb 7, 2010 at 3:40 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Echo Station 57, we're on our way....slowly

As Ralphee says the live action prop speeder had those side supports, but the ILM filming models didn't and that's what I based my kit on. As you can see in this pic they haven't even got Lukes' grey markings on the airbrake box! -pretty major continuity error really!

NB: I did incorporate a few aspects of the live action cockpit to make the kit a bit more interesting and lend more scope for people to superdetails.

Nick

────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Echo Station 57, we're on our way....slowly

Well, i got a kit a few days ago, at least, i got a hull set, the other parts are due to me in the AM from the US.

Anybody else building this so far...anybody else have the same god awful casting of hulls i do? I do mean....AWFUL.

I mean, a few air bubbles isnt the end of the world, but this thing, well it may as well be porous......i dont think there is one clean panel line meaning much of it ill have to fill and re scribe.

Oh and anybody else noticing, that MUCH of the model, is in fact idealised, and pretty far (at least from a donor aspect) from accurate?

Many parts are already being found, that are total easy pickings...so i find it hard there not present on the cast parts....which im still yet to eyeball tomorrow.....exctiement....more like sheer dread....yup, money well spent.

Pics to come as i need to blow some primer on this, so i can show how bad things really are....airbrake boxes look nice though.....and i hear the decals rock....so not a bad deal at all!

lee

Post #443  (forum post #1145074)
Author    : Gort
Date      : Mar 1, 2010 at 12:12 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Echo Station 57, we're on our way....slowly

Hi Lee,

You backed out of my list, so I never actually sold you a kit? - I never professed to have got all the parts despite asking on the forum here. Some times I got help, often though people couldn't offer any suggestions. So in some areas I had to do the best I could.

I did get enough kit parts and good reference to make it proportionally very accurate...in my opinion. I posted countless pictures of my progress so that when the time came to sell the kits everyone had seen what I had done. I was even complimented, possibly by youreslf on offering such high rez pics.

The Hulls have been a struggle for me to make. But I would hope they are not awful. Not sure how you came by yours?

Anyway, this seems a good point for me to announce that as of now I've stopped producing the Snowspeeder kit. Another talented member far better equipped to handle the production of the kit will be taking over soon and will carry on with client list in the order that I have it so no one will lose out. The turnaround time on kits will be MUCH faster that I could ever do so people will also get kits far more quickly. He will also carry on additional kit bashing work to finally clear up the odd areas that need more work.

So that's it. No more garage kits for me. ( is that a cheer I hear from Lee!)Good luck to everyone with all their various projects. I shall leave this thread in the capable hands of another, who can announce his plans to you in his own time.

Signing out for the last time................

N

The hull is being fully replicated in styrene from your dims....im just taking the measures and copying it onto 2mm HIPS (what a pain in the butt that is) itll take me around the same time to rebuild the hull, as it would to clean the resin one up...and seeing as im adding RC to the flaps, id rather it be a clean sweep.

I realise the guys who have kits are happy, fair play to them, but i have higher standards in afraid.

Heres to hoping Steve can knock this one out well, im sure he will, and in the meantime, any parts that i find along the way, that were missed or scratched on the original master, ill be shooting them over to him.

lee

Post #449  (forum post #1150533)
Author    : Gort
Date      : Mar 6, 2010 at 9:04 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Echo Station 57, we're on our way....slowly

Thanks for the support guys.

A few weeks ago it became clear that as we need to move out of where we are to save money I would be without a workshop for about a year. As its also taking me far too long IMO to make the kits, it seemed the best thing to sell on the project and enable those who want a kit to get one alot faster than they would if I was still doing it.

Steve and I have yet to actually complete the deal but I expect to get it all sorted in the next few days. What will be a V2 Speeder should incorporate the accuracy that I feel we have got with the proportions ( Thanks to Dan Satterthwaite for help with the dims) ,and a fresh level of kit bashing. I will be helping Steve do a new set of instructions as I've had very good feedback over the ones I've done for the V1 Speeder.

Steve is also better set up to resin cast the hulls which will ensure greater lightness and consistancy. - Lee if you've got a bad set of hulls from somewhere I'm sorry. I've had good feedback from others. I was applying epoxy during a very cold spell on a couple of kits and it didn't always work in as well as I would have liked. No excuse, but that's all I can think of it being.

Anyway, I will be building again but for a while my workshop will be packed away in storage. I'm thinking I will look to doing more one off stuff for collectors rather than production runs. 

Cheers

Nick

Post #452  (forum post #1150763)
Author    : swpropmaker
Date      : Mar 6, 2010 at 1:41 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Echo Station 57, we're on our way....slowly

Guys… I will be finalizing the transaction with Nick in the next few days… Nick has attempted to pull off a huge kit in his first production run!  I congratulate him on his effort!  I will be taking over the run as it exists now.  However like the Tydirium Shuttle we will make an attempt to place more accurate details on the replica before making molds.    I have a few ideas on making the hulls one piece roto cast and still allow entry to the interior by making most of the rear details plant ons to the joined roto cast hull.    I’m not sure any production run can meet the accuracy that a 1 of studio model but I will endeavor  to  make the snow speeder as accurate as possible.  I will stick to Nicks list and once patterns are dressed and molds are made I will attempt to ship 5 a week until the list is complete.  Questions.. please pm or email me directly sneisen@bresnan.net

Steve

Re: Echo Station 57, we're on our way....slowly

Today I have received a kit for Wedge Version.

Wooow, the casting is great! There is only minor cleanup work required and I might just do some tiny touch up work to some parts.

Packing, decals, instructions, magnets etc. - everything is just outstanding. It is clearly visible that a huge amount of time and knowledge went into this kit.

This kit is absolutely fantastic !!! I highly recommend it.

I know that even with the greatest kit, there is always some room for improvments. This kit is not 100% studio accurate due to a few doner parts that have not been used. But it is so damn close to the studio model, that I can easily live with that. For me, the kit I have received is perfect and I am looking forward to building it.

Since I saw the first pics of Nicks masters, I was full of anticipating joy and so I have ordered 3 kits. Having received such a wonderful first kit and knowing that the other two will be casted by Steve makes be absolutely sure that buying 3 was an excellent descision. Today I am totally happy and looking forward to 2 more kits.

Nick, THANK YOU VERY VERY MUCH !!!

Michael

Post #519  (forum post #1324560)
Author    : mslz22
Date      : Aug 9, 2010 at 7:01 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Echo Station 57, we're on our way....slowly

Hey Guys, just wanted to chime in with a few things about the test build and a few more pics now that shipping has begun.  

One of the most important things to note about the castings is that in I separated a couple parts in the interest of getting them easier to cast, or in some cases configured in a way that the casting would be better.  The 2 major places this happened was on the forward gun mounts to body mounts and also on the air brake boxes to rear gun mount parts.  When i separated the parts for casting, rather than clean up the glue marks at the separation point I left it as is for ease of proper registration when they are glued back together for assembly of the kit.  I was afraid that if i cleaned up the parts I may lose the registration location, and the positioning of these parts is really important.  I mention this because it looks a little sloppy on the casting, so i had mixed feelings about it, but when i put the kit together the parts really almost just "click" back together.  I just held them together and put a drop of thin superglue in non visible spot and the parts were easily recombined.  

Again, I mention the above because I had to make a choice between what i thought looked good and what i thought would make assembly easier, and i chose to go with ease of assembly. So any of the separation marks you see not only act as alignment markers, they also get completely covered up in assembly.

I will be posting a bit more as i have time over the next day or so, but i will say that it is important to store the main body parts appropriately until you are able to get some of the main structures together, the main body castings are thin enough that until you start adding the support structures like the airbrake boxes/gun mounts etc the outer edges of the upper and lower bodies will be prone to warping if not stored correctly.   

Once the support structures are in place and the top and bottom are combined none of that should be an issue,  in fact i intentionally warped the top body on the one you see here by leaning it up against the wall on a 100 degree day and once i started adding structures it all pulled back into place, in fact I did not even need to heat it back up, once you start gluing parts in place there is a lamination effect that straightens things up, and strengthens the whole thing.

Some more pics of my test shot which is still a WIP, i will post some more assembly tips in the next few days.

thanks

mike

Post #525  (forum post #1324979)
Author    : 3d-builder
Date      : Aug 10, 2010 at 6:52 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Echo Station 57, we're on our way....slowly

I think mike made some great points inherently the hulls 

of the speeder are going to be weak it's just part of that shape

and design. I noticed once adding the canopy things strengthened 

up, but even then I couldn't do it without the top hull being taped

down  at the correct height first. I also noticed it was nearly impossible

to make the canopy  separate and cut out all the view screens

and then get it sit up in the hull!!:angry Every time I cut the screens out

the canopy would weaken and change shape, so I had to build it up

on the hull and glue as I went.Then I came back and cut out the screens 

as it was locked in place.

[IMAGE: MVC-008S.jpg]

At that point if your going to sit it down you still have to tape the sides, abd yes the boxes will add some definite support as mike said, but i would still

suggest keeping it taped down!

[IMAGE: MVC-913S.jpg]

[IMAGE: MVC-927S.jpg]

This is the rear bulkhead and it's just a paper template for the part

that I cut out in 3mm styrene, once it's fitted the top hull is rock

solid and you can set it down on it's own weight!:thumbsup

[IMAGE: MVC-935S.jpg]

[IMAGE: MVC-936S.jpg]

Here it is in plastic ready to be glued in place.

[IMAGE: MVC-938S.jpg]

Post #544  (forum post #1332287)
Author    : mslz22
Date      : Aug 16, 2010 at 10:15 AM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Re: Echo Station 57, we're on our way....slowly

Thanks, believe it or not it's just a spray bomb with the Testors flat light aircraft gray, about a can and a half.  The orange is good old reefer orange, accent panels were done with equipment gray primer from walmart for the slightly darker ones and Krylon fusion Pewter gray for the lighter gray.  I was hesitant about using the Testors stuff at first but to my eye it's a pretty good match for the studio model once i did a highly diluted wash with some ivory black oil color.

Thanks 

mike
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
Post #545  (forum post #1336524)
Author    : REL
Date      : Aug 19, 2010 at 3:20 PM
────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────

Thanks, Mike. 

Just one recommendation I would have for anyone building these is to reinforce the edge on the top fuselage. The resin is thin there because it has to be to maintain that sharp thin edge, but unfortunately, especially in the heat of summer, it wants to get wavy and warp out to shape. 

It's an easy fix to get the edge straight again with a heat gun or hot water, but to make sure it stays that way I used some aluminum bar and epoxied it in place. It really strengthens the edge to where you almost can't bend it.

[IMAGE: tf_spdr_01.jpg]

 

[IMAGE: tf_spdr_02.jpg]
